<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_917dc549-9c1e-4599-ba9c-ee7d35fd5782'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer9914866827296438462">Medical resident Dr. Abby Matteo is elated when the elite cardiac transplant team at Boston's Bayside Hospital taps her as a potential recruit. But faced with a tormenting life-and-death decision, Abby helps direct a crash victim's harvested heart to a dying teenager -- instead of the wealthy older woman who was supposed to receive it. The repercussions leave Abby shaken a</span>
  <span id="freeText9914866827296438462" style="display:none">Medical resident Dr. Abby Matteo is elated when the elite cardiac transplant team at Boston's Bayside Hospital taps her as a potential recruit. But faced with a tormenting life-and-death decision, Abby helps direct a crash victim's harvested heart to a dying teenager -- instead of the wealthy older woman who was supposed to receive it. The repercussions leave Abby shaken and plagued with self-doubt.<br /><br />Suddenly, a new heart appears, and the woman's transplant is completed. Then Abby makes a terrible discovery. The donor records have been falsified -- the new heart has not come through the proper channels. Defying the hospital's demands for silence, she begins her own investigation that reveals a murderous, unthinkable conspiracy. Every move Abby makes spawns a vicious backlash...and on a ship anchored in the waters of Boston harbor, the grisly truth lies waiting.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_195480199" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195480199" />
    <a title="Brenda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2337007-brenda"><img alt="Brenda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577750190p2/2337007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195480199?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda" href="/user/show/2337007-brenda">Brenda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553817720" href="/book/show/629479.Harvest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=medical">medical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195480199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14884728562906259467">Dr Abby DiMatteo felt like she was in a good place; a second year resident at Bayside Hospital, and working with the elite cardiac transplant team – she was just beginning to feel that all her hard work, the study, the years of staying at home when her friends went out partying and her huge student debt; it was all worth it. <br/><br/>With the devastating loss of a female car crash victim, brain dead but healthy in every other aspect it meant, with the husband’s permission, the heart was ready to be harve</span>
  <span id="freeText14884728562906259467" style="display:none">Dr Abby DiMatteo felt like she was in a good place; a second year resident at Bayside Hospital, and working with the elite cardiac transplant team – she was just beginning to feel that all her hard work, the study, the years of staying at home when her friends went out partying and her huge student debt; it was all worth it. <br /><br />With the devastating loss of a female car crash victim, brain dead but healthy in every other aspect it meant, with the husband’s permission, the heart was ready to be harvested to save a critically ill patient. The wealthy Nina Voss was the recipient, but Abby was confronted by the fact that a seventeen year old boy would also die without this heart. The decision Abby made in that emotional moment of matching the heart to the two different patients suddenly had her facing the intense rage of an extremely wealthy man – a man who could buy anything he wanted; a man who would also <b>do</b> anything to get what he wanted. <br /><br />Suddenly Abby’s world tilted on its axis. Something was wrong – desperately wrong. As she began a covert investigation into hospital files and past transplants, she wondered who she could trust. What about Mark, her brand new fiancé – she should be able to trust him, shouldn’t she? But the intricate web of deceit and deception went deep; Abby was in danger and didn’t know where to turn. Would anyone help her? Or was she in way over her head? <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this dark psychological medical thriller. Author Tess Gerritsen never disappoints. The plot was fast paced and full of intrigue, with twists and turns until the very end. Gripping, twisted and full of a terror that what was happening in this fictional book could be actually happening out there in the real world. I have no hesitation in recommending <i>Harvest</i> highly.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14884728562906259467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This book grabbed my attention immediately and I just did not want to pull myself away.<br /><br />The story centers on medical resident Abby DiMatteo, an ambitious new surgeon. Amidst the stress and sleep deprivation of her job at the hospital, she finds herself stumbling into irregularities with her hospital's transpant team. More specifically, organs seem to be coming available without the usual documentation. She starts to investigate and her search leads her into a dark underworld of corruption and some of the more horrifying aspects of the organ trade. This dark, action-packed story is one of Gerritsen's earliest thrillers and even though parts of it are a tad predictable, it was still a fantastic read.</span>

<div id="review_36881867" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36881867" />
    <a title="Sheree" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1612410-sheree"><img alt="Sheree" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264544762p2/1612410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36881867?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheree" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheree" href="/user/show/1612410-sheree">Sheree</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1612410-sheree?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1612410-sheree?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1612410-sheree?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1612410-sheree?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36881867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7455089945576666403">This is Tess Gerritsen's first medical thriller, prior to this she wrote romance. Gerritsen a Doctor, left her profession to concentrate on writing & raising her children. I laughed out loud at the manner in which Tess reports on her blog, the awful comments she gets from fans who love her medical thrillers then sample her romance novels. She tells writers and I think this applies to readers as well - "be prepared when you switch genres." <br/>"Thriller writers hunger for respect from the mystery wor</span>
  <span id="freeText7455089945576666403" style="display:none">This is Tess Gerritsen's first medical thriller, prior to this she wrote romance. Gerritsen a Doctor, left her profession to concentrate on writing &amp; raising her children. I laughed out loud at the manner in which Tess reports on her blog, the awful comments she gets from fans who love her medical thrillers then sample her romance novels. She tells writers and I think this applies to readers as well - "be prepared when you switch genres." <br />"Thriller writers hunger for respect from the mystery world. Mystery writers want respect from the literary world. <br />And romance authors — heck, they’d just like to stop being dumped on." <br />Anyway on with my review, Tess Gerritsen's medical experience shows in her writing, in her mastery of surgical &amp; medical technical details, making for a vivid, authentic &amp; believable story.<br />The Organ Transplant Team at a Boston Hospital is interested in promising surgical resident Abby DiMatteo. Transplant matches are conveniently appearing &amp; wealthy private patients are receiving donor organs ahead of patients with a more urgent medical need.<br />When Dr DiMatteo bucks the system a sinister web of corruption and horror is revealed. The reader makes a connection early on that the Russian orphans being bought and sold are not going to America for adoption or a trip to Disneyland. However connecting the dots does not in anyway detract from the page-turning horror &amp; suspense; twists &amp; turns right to the last page kept me enthralled. <br />The most horrifying element in 'Harvest' is knowing what prompted Gerritsen to write this novel - do some research those reviewers who don't believe this is a plausible story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7455089945576666403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_111483400" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111483400" />
    <a title="Linda Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2613351-linda-robinson"><img alt="Linda Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588091170p2/2613351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111483400?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda Robinson" href="/user/show/2613351-linda-robinson">Linda Robinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671553012" href="/book/show/2046183.Harvest">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111483400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9234184044863168262">Maybe I'll break my rule about reading the first novel by an author I haven't read before. The first is new work, a writer getting their writing muscles warmed up, the first editorial relationship tested, working arrangements, word choices being set like a table for a fancy dinner. This first novel has no tablecloth and plastic forks; we know the set-up, the bad guys, and the outcome way too soon. There's a weird typo missed in a sentence early on that read "opened the 'chest,'" instead of "char</span>
  <span id="freeText9234184044863168262" style="display:none">Maybe I'll break my rule about reading the first novel by an author I haven't read before. The first is new work, a writer getting their writing muscles warmed up, the first editorial relationship tested, working arrangements, word choices being set like a table for a fancy dinner. This first novel has no tablecloth and plastic forks; we know the set-up, the bad guys, and the outcome way too soon. There's a weird typo missed in a sentence early on that read "opened the 'chest,'" instead of "chart." It was hard not to study the manuscript too intensely from that point on, because the story isn't a feast that makes you forget about the accoutrement. The story's been done before; only the names of characters have been changed. It's good writing, especially concerning the children. But it's just too easy to have a female hero who trips over her own feet, makes silly - and then stupid - decisions, gets herself caught more than once, and cries too damn much; and always, always preceded by "I won't cry. I won't!" after which she does. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9234184044863168262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_361287654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/361287654" />
    <a title="Terri Lynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5699299-terri-lynn"><img alt="Terri Lynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329255932p2/5699299.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/361287654?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terri Lynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terri Lynn" href="/user/show/5699299-terri-lynn">Terri Lynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671553012" href="/book/show/2046183.Harvest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5699299-terri-lynn?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5699299-terri-lynn?shelf=mystery-suspense-thrillers">mystery-suspense-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361287654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7329389388553482801">I can't believe I read this in less than 24 hours. All 344 pages! This story was so good and so fast-paced, I couldn't stop. <br/><br/>Tess Gerritsen, like another favorite of mine Robin Cook, is a physician so writing a medical mystery comes natural to her. <br/><br/>Dr. Abby DiMatteo is a second year resident at Boston's Bayside Hospital. After 4 years of college and 4 years of medical school, she is finally getting to do what she longed to do since losing her beloved little brother as a child- surgery. She is al</span>
  <span id="freeText7329389388553482801" style="display:none">I can't believe I read this in less than 24 hours. All 344 pages! This story was so good and so fast-paced, I couldn't stop. <br /><br />Tess Gerritsen, like another favorite of mine Robin Cook, is a physician so writing a medical mystery comes natural to her. <br /><br />Dr. Abby DiMatteo is a second year resident at Boston's Bayside Hospital. After 4 years of college and 4 years of medical school, she is finally getting to do what she longed to do since losing her beloved little brother as a child- surgery. She is also living with forty-something surgeon Mark Hodell who also works at Bayside.<br /><br />I really liked the character of Abby. She is the kind of person you'd like to have as your doctor and your friend. Ditto for Dr.Vivian Chao . Dr. Chao works in the 5th year residency with clinic patients who are uninsured and while she's not the openly warm and fuzzy type, you can see her heart for the poor and uninsured. She is smart as a whip and has very fast hands in surgery. These two women are great characters.<br /><br />Problems erupt when a woman who is AB positive is left brain dead after an accident where a drunken idiot crashes head on into her while driving down the wrong side of the road. The heart really should go to the person at the top of the transplant list which is a teen boy under Dr. Chao's care. Instead, a rich and vindictive SOB named Victor Voss tries to purchase the heart right out from under the boy for his dying 46 year old wife Nina Voss (the only person on the planet who can stand him and not that much!). <br /><br />The hospital admin is going along with the sale . Vivian is watching the boy code over and over. Finally, she transfers him to Mass General. She sends Abby to the husband of the woman who the heart is being harvested from to sign a directed donation giving the heart to the boy. The man signs and then Abby is sent in an ambulance to courier the heart to the other hospital. The hospital director tries to get the ambulance back but she gets there and the heart is implanted and the boy is saved.<br /><br />Meanwhile, the hospital administrator, the transplant director, the lawyer, and the head of the residency program are royally pissed and Abby must face them. Vivian has been fired but since she has already done her residency, she can just get a job in a practice. Abby is just a second year resident and barely manages to hold on to her job. <br /><br />A furious Victor Voss wants to see heads roll. The main head he wants to see roll is Abby's and as the 14th richest man in America, he can afford to see it happen. First, he has a Russian boy murdered for his heart for Nina then takes out in a reign of terror after Abby. When Abby finds her fiance Mark is involved and the Russian Mafia are transporting orphans to murder to harvest for body parts, she hooks up with the detective investigating her- Detective Katzka- for the ride of her life. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7329389388553482801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20306725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18122117145596519435">In one of Tess Gerritsen's earlier medical thrillers, Harvest dealt with organ transplantation and the darker side of it. When Dr. Abby Matteo, a medical resident, was elated to find out she was a potential recruit for the Boston Bayside Hospital's transport team, she was in for a ride. As she helped deliver a heart to a dying teen than an elderly woman who needed it, guilt wracked her. And when a new heart arrived for the woman, she discovered a shocking truth of the cover-up of falsified donor</span>
  <span id="freeText18122117145596519435" style="display:none">In one of Tess Gerritsen's earlier medical thrillers, Harvest dealt with organ transplantation and the darker side of it. When Dr. Abby Matteo, a medical resident, was elated to find out she was a potential recruit for the Boston Bayside Hospital's transport team, she was in for a ride. As she helped deliver a heart to a dying teen than an elderly woman who needed it, guilt wracked her. And when a new heart arrived for the woman, she discovered a shocking truth of the cover-up of falsified donor records. As the hospital wanted her to keep it a secret, she went on her own medical investigation to discover the grisly side of it, when she ended up on unchartered waters to face a deadly killer. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18122117145596519435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9166041940866955226">Reading this book makes me feel like my neck being squeezed. The pressure keeps building page by page. Now I'm nearing suffocation. But it's a good suffocation. I don't know. Maybe I'm experiencing literary erotic aphyxiation. While dying to be released of this torture, I still want more. Gerritsen doesn't hold back on grusome.   <span id="freeText9166041940866955226" style="display:none">Reading this book makes me feel like my neck being squeezed. The pressure keeps building page by page. Now I'm nearing suffocation. But it's a good suffocation. I don't know. Maybe I'm experiencing literary erotic aphyxiation. While dying to be released of this torture, I still want more. Gerritsen doesn't hold back on grusome. Abby was deliberately/wrongfully accused of mentally unstable. I suspect she would actually be so for real after the ordeal she suffers at the end of the book. The villains are so over-the-top and, considering they're supposed to be smart people, I find some of their actions unreasonably risky and unnecessarily evil.<br /> <br />In conclusion, Harvest is a very suspenseful page-turner. If you can get past the believable factor, it is a great pick to pass your time.</span>

<div id="review_2281859929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2281859929" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1080270-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208136693p2/1080270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2281859929?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1080270-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281859929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8667286424678204811">This book is not the kind of book I usually read. I only read it because I LOVE the television show Rizzoli and Isles and this is the same author. I love the show because the main characters are strong independent women, not afraid to grab life by the horns. Awesome female role models. This book is the same. The women may struggle but they never give up. They are intelligent, capable and they do not use men as crutches. Also, I actually listened to this book. I listened during the ride home, the</span>
  <span id="freeText8667286424678204811" style="display:none">This book is not the kind of book I usually read. I only read it because I LOVE the television show Rizzoli and Isles and this is the same author. I love the show because the main characters are strong independent women, not afraid to grab life by the horns. Awesome female role models. This book is the same. The women may struggle but they never give up. They are intelligent, capable and they do not use men as crutches. Also, I actually listened to this book. I listened during the ride home, then while making dinner. I took the reading into the bathroom. I never turned on the TV. I stayed up much later than usual. Then I took it with me to bed. Every night I like to tuck myself into bed with a good audio book and usually by that point it puts me right to sleep. Most of my actual 'reading' happens in the car, or when I am at least mostly vertical. That was not the case with this book. I stayed awake. It was riveting and always surprising. I was too upset for the main character to force her to wait for resolution while I slept. I do not regret my lack of sleep. I cannot say enough for this book and this author! I started another book by the same author today. I hope I get some sleep tonight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8667286424678204811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6679597653115758178" style="display:none">It wasn’t my first Tess Gerritsen novel so I had high expectation for this one. And I wasn’t disappointed. It was really written, the characters were engaging enough for me to like them. Especially Aleksiej and Yakov. I felt some kind of fear for them while reading the book. So when one of them died I literally started crying. <br />But the book had some flaws. For me the main problem with it was the fact that I was kinda bored while reading the first half of this book. The real action starts in the second half so if you don’t have patience for such book it’s not a novel for you. <br />But for me it is still worth reading because of the characters.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2631767003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2066485984905388546">,,Harvest'' by Tess Gerritsen is the first book by this author which is not Rizzoli and Isles aeries but grapped my attention in a total way. I really read it in almost in one sitting. Although I was very liesitating taking this book because the main hero wasn't Jane or Maura. To my amusement Abby DiMatteo was not even am ambitious surgeon grapped me completely. Young, inteligent, suspicious was a perfect heroine. <br/>''Harvest'' focuses on organ transplants and the story involves organ donation on </span>
  <span id="freeText2066485984905388546" style="display:none">,,Harvest'' by Tess Gerritsen is the first book by this author which is not Rizzoli and Isles aeries but grapped my attention in a total way. I really read it in almost in one sitting. Although I was very liesitating taking this book because the main hero wasn't Jane or Maura. To my amusement Abby DiMatteo was not even am ambitious surgeon grapped me completely. Young, inteligent, suspicious was a perfect heroine. <br />''Harvest'' focuses on organ transplants and the story involves organ donation on the black market. When I was reading yhis novel I felt I was involved in the profession of surgeons. All in all this medical thriller is so captivating you cannot stop turning pages until the end. That's why I was really astonished that ''Harvest'' was the first Tess Gerritsen's medical thriller because it doesn't seem like. It is difficult to believe that prior to it Gerritsen was writting romances. You can see author's medical experience in this book. That's why this full of medical and surgical details story is authentically believable. </span>

<div id="review_1659261828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1659261828" />
    <a title="Angela Meadon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5838164-angela-meadon"><img alt="Angela Meadon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447400839p2/5838164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1659261828?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela Meadon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela Meadon" href="/user/show/5838164-angela-meadon">Angela Meadon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1659261828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14248376269305499380">It has been a very long time since I read a medical thriller. In fact, some of the first adult books I ever read were Robin Cook’s wonderful medical thrillers. I read them in my early teens, somewhere between my Dean Koontz binge and my first exposure to Robert Jordan.<br/><br/>As with so many good things in life, I’ve found my way back to medical thrillers with Tess Gerritsen’s Harvest.<br/><br/>This is Gerritsen’s first medical thriller (I understand that she wrote romance before this novel), and I’m incredibly p</span>
  <span id="freeText14248376269305499380" style="display:none">It has been a very long time since I read a medical thriller. In fact, some of the first adult books I ever read were Robin Cook’s wonderful medical thrillers. I read them in my early teens, somewhere between my Dean Koontz binge and my first exposure to Robert Jordan.<br /><br />As with so many good things in life, I’ve found my way back to medical thrillers with Tess Gerritsen’s Harvest.<br /><br />This is Gerritsen’s first medical thriller (I understand that she wrote romance before this novel), and I’m incredibly pleased that she made the change. I picked up Harvest on the recommendation of friends in my Facebook book club, and I was hooked from the first page. I’ve been going through something of a reading drought over the past year or so, picking up books only to get bored quickly and move on to something else. Well, I finished Harvest in a weekend and promptly bought another Gerritsen novel. What did I enjoy so much? Let me tell you.<br /><br />It has all the ingredients of a great medical thriller: A smart doctor who faces utter ruination, both personal and professional, incredibly high stakes, and deep medical moral questions (who get’s the valuable organs?).<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this novel. It moves along at a blistering pace, drawing the doomed Dr Matteo ever deeper into the web of lies and suspicion. I especially enjoyed the counter-point POV offered by the young Russian boy on the ship headed for America. And the way Gerritsen wove their two stories together in the end, while a little predictable, was wonderfully satisfying.<br /><br />I say the book was predictable, and it was in some ways. However, I think that Gerritsen made enough of the twists her own for the novel to avoid falling into trope hell. Yes, she ticks the boxes for a thriller, but she does it with flair and skill that means I didn’t really mind. I walked away from this book with a deep appreciation of Tess Gerritsen’s ability as a masterful storyteller, and a re-discovered love for a genre that I cut my teeth on.<br /><br />Personally, this book has lit a bonfire of creative inspiration in my head. I can think of no greater book than one that makes me feel passionate about writing.<br /><br />Two thumbs, way up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14248376269305499380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/LBv7cQ/6S/w+lOabtFerg+OBE4ihXQE7+EqLjeeTmWbx0RnRZZo8KLnYXpRL2ufNZluY7Lm0ysTFDMcTyij2A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DiBXusmoW4JB8aaFapNk9lQIGA7cJFNPvZRDobmcCb5pV3wwSAHaXRPslGVVbVHHbh9yI0xH9GBBYVqTwSrkAw==')})
  }

Το μπαρ στη Μέιν Στρητ είναι άψογο, το εστιατόριο σερβίρει το καλύτερο φαγητό της πολιτείας, η ιδιοκτήτρια της πανσιόν είναι ελκυστική και το χαμόγελό της ακαταμάχητο. Όλα θα ήταν ειδυλλιακά, αν δεν είχε εξαφανιστεί εδώ και τέσσερα εικοσιτετράωρα εκείνο το κορίτσι. \n\nΤο απόσπασμα που θα οργανωθεί θα βρει τελικά την Όμπρεϊ Χάρισον, αλλά θα τη βρει νεκρή, εγκλωβισμένη σε μια φυσική παγίδα των βράχων έξω από την πόλη. Παρά τη σιγουριά του τοπικού σερίφη για το αντίθετο, ο νεοφερμένος ντετέκτιβ είναι βέβαιος πως δεν πρόκειται για ατύχημα. Γιατί πριν πεθάνει η Όμπρεϊ Χάρισον προσπάθησε να κόψει μόνη το ίδιο της το πόδι. Με έναν ελβετικό σουγιά. \n\nΠολύ σύντομα θα φανεί πως στο Φόλσβιλ υπάρχουν μυστικά και ένα παρελθόν που όλοι θέλουν να το κρατήσουν θαμμένο. Ο Μπεν Λόγκαν, όμως, δε θα ησυχάσει μέχρι να βρει το δολοφόνο του κοριτσιού. \n\nΘα το πάει στα άκρα.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"18168547668898734628\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));;       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18149.Tess_Gerritsen">About Tess Gerritsen</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17147866508614801357">Internationally bestselling author Tess Gerritsen took an unusual route to a writing career. A graduate of Stanford University, Tess went on to medical school at the University of California, San Francisco, where she was awarded her M.D.<br/><br/>While on maternity leave from her work as a physician, she began to write fiction. In 1987, her first novel was published. Call After Midnight, a romantic thriller</span>
  <span id="freeText17147866508614801357" style="display:none">Internationally bestselling author Tess Gerritsen took an unusual route to a writing career. A graduate of Stanford University, Tess went on to medical school at the University of California, San Francisco, where she was awarded her M.D.<br /><br />While on maternity leave from her work as a physician, she began to write fiction. In 1987, her first novel was published. Call After Midnight, a romantic thriller, was followed by eight more romantic suspense novels. She also wrote a screenplay, "Adrift", which aired as a 1993 CBS Movie of the Week starring Kate Jackson.<br /><br />Tess's first medical thriller, Harvest, was released in hardcover in 1996, and it marked her debut on the New York Times bestseller list. Her suspense novels since then have been: Life Support (1997), Bloodstream (1998), Gravity (1999), The Surgeon (2001), The Apprentice (2002), The Sinner (2003), Body Double (2004), Vanish (2005), The Mephisto Club (2006), and The Bone Garden (2007). Her books have been translated into 31 languages, and more than 15 million copies have been sold around the world.<br /><br />As well as being a New York Times bestselling author, she has also been a #1 bestseller in both Germany and the UK. She has won both the Nero Wolfe Award (for Vanish) and the Rita Award (for The Surgeon.) Critics around the world have praised her novels as "Pulse-pounding fun" (Philadelphia Inquirer), "Scary and brilliant" (Toronto Globe and Mail), and "Polished, riveting prose" (Chicago Tribune). Publisher Weekly has dubbed her the "medical suspense queen".<br /><br />Now retired from medicine, she writes full time. She lives in Maine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17147866508614801357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
